    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1934888833" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1934888833" />
    <a title="Jill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6638317-jill"><img alt="Jill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368732701p2/6638317.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1934888833?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jill" href="/user/show/6638317-jill">Jill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1934888833" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12550180461008312426">I have a soft spot for dark books. I have a particularly soft spot for dark books written at a time when they weren't acceptable. In some ways, with the screaming for moral purity hitting both sides of the political spectrum, we are heading that way again.<br/><br/>So: all the more reason to read fiction that breaks.<br/><br/>I read this in a day, in Stockholm, glancing in the direction of places and neighbourhoods as they were mentioned. Something writhed in this narrative: obviously, the thoughts of a twisted, re</span>
  <span id="freeText12550180461008312426" style="display:none">I have a soft spot for dark books. I have a particularly soft spot for dark books written at a time when they weren't acceptable. In some ways, with the screaming for moral purity hitting both sides of the political spectrum, we are heading that way again.<br /><br />So: all the more reason to read fiction that breaks.<br /><br />I read this in a day, in Stockholm, glancing in the direction of places and neighbourhoods as they were mentioned. Something writhed in this narrative: obviously, the thoughts of a twisted, repressed turn-of-the-century mind, but something else ---<br /><br />This is the delicately sociopathic portrait of a man who doesn't love, probably can't love, but can obsess. And the twist is that when he finds his object of obsession, his goal is not to hurt, but to <i>save</i> her. Murder is on the table, of course, but not when it comes to her. The complexity and subjectivity of morality, here, is expressly highlighted in the text, in pleasant conversations Glas has with his peers. Vigilante justice: we've been obsessing over that one for a loooong time. This is an earlier example, and a subtler one, and it hits hard.<br /><br />Plus: Stockholm. Shit. &lt;3</span>
  <a data-text-id="12550180461008312426" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1125028412" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1125028412" />
    <a title="Cecilia H." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34146082-cecilia-h"><img alt="Cecilia H." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556446940p2/34146082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1125028412?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cecilia H." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cecilia H." href="/user/show/34146082-cecilia-h">Cecilia H.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789100581527" href="/book/show/10780909-doktor-glas">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34146082-cecilia-h?shelf=swedish-literature">swedish-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34146082-cecilia-h?shelf=3-stars-and-a-half">3-stars-and-a-half</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34146082-cecilia-h?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34146082-cecilia-h?shelf=reviewed-books">reviewed-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1125028412" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9080059405177413676">Real rating *~. --> <b>3,5</b> <-- .~*<br/><br/>Wow! This book is really modern for the time it was published - 1905. I'm impressed, amazed and also a bit scared by Hjalmar Söderberg. Haha!<br/><br/>The main character in Doctor Glas, Doktor Glas in Swedish (Glas means glass) is of course a Doctor named Glas. Throughout the book, he deals with moral issues and love.<br/> Glas falls madly in love with one of his patients, a woman named Helga Gregorius. She is (of course) married to a pastor. But Helga is not happily married. She</span>
  <span id="freeText9080059405177413676" style="display:none">Real rating *~. --&gt; <b>3,5</b> &lt;-- .~*<br /><br />Wow! This book is really modern for the time it was published - 1905. I'm impressed, amazed and also a bit scared by Hjalmar Söderberg. Haha!<br /><br />The main character in Doctor Glas, Doktor Glas in Swedish (Glas means glass) is of course a Doctor named Glas. Throughout the book, he deals with moral issues and love.<br /> Glas falls madly in love with one of his patients, a woman named Helga Gregorius. She is (of course) married to a pastor. But Helga is not happily married. She hates her husband who is described as a horrible person. Pastor Gregorius is ugly, morally corrupt and sleeps with his wife without her approval. Helga asks Glas for help in stopping the pastor from harassing her. Glas decides to help the young woman and falls in love with her too. But Helga is already involved with another man besides her husband. As time goes by in the book, Glas loves Helga more and more and gets more and more crazy. He then begins to consider <b>if he should kill pastor Gregorius</b> to free Helga...<br /><br />I really liked the questions this book deals with. The character Doctor Glas was everything from a <u>genius</u> to <u>brilliant</u> to a <u>madman</u>. Some parts of the book were just unbelievable and sure got me thinking!<br /> I wanted to give this book 4 stars first but sometimes it was a bit tiresome to read so it gets 3,5! ;) But I highly recommend you to read this one!<br /><br />Some extracts from the book:<br />- These are in Swedish because I read it in Swedish, but if you want to read them in English: translate with help from something/someone (or ask me and I will try to make it good :) ) or just read the book!<br /><br /><b>~ s. 50 ~</b> (OM MORAL)<br /><i>"Aldrig har jag haft en så stark känsla av att moralen är en karusell, som går runt. Det visste jag egentligen förut, men jag hade alltid tänkt mig, att svängningstiderna måste vara sekler eller tidevarv - nu föreföllo de mig som minuter och sekunder."</i><br /><br /><b>~ s. 59 ~</b> (OM SKÄRGÅRDEN)<br /><i>"Jag tycker inte så mycket om varken bekanta eller villor eller skärgården. Framför allt inte skärgården. Ett landskap hackat till kalops. Små holmar, små vatten, små bergsknallar och små mariga träd. Ett blekt och fattigt landskap, kallt i färgen, mest grått och blått, och likväl inte fattigt nog att äga ödslighetens storhet."</i><br /><br /><b>~ s. 156 ~</b> (SPECIALARE)<br /><i>"Vem var det som sade: 'Livet är kort, men timmarna äro långa.' Det borde ha varit en matematiker som Pascal, men det var visst Fénélon. Synd, att det inte var jag."</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9080059405177413676" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_193799794" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/193799794" />
    <a title="Fia Eamónn Wåhlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5949904-fia-eam-nn-w-hlin"><img alt="Fia Eamónn Wåhlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312414866p2/5949904.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/193799794?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fia Eamónn Wåhlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fia Eamónn Wåhlin" href="/user/show/5949904-fia-eam-nn-w-hlin">Fia Eamónn Wåhlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer193799794" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17617073320929258283">Doktor Glas is a short but a very intense book about a doctor in Sweden whose life we follow through his journals, we learn about his thoughts and life. You soon meet Mrs Gregorius, a young beautiful woman who is married to a pastor, significant older than her. She goes to doktor Glas about her troubles of carrying out her wifely duties in the bedroom, she is inlove with another man but trapped in a loveless marriage and is basically forced to be intimate with her husband every night. And finall</span>
  <span id="freeText17617073320929258283" style="display:none">Doktor Glas is a short but a very intense book about a doctor in Sweden whose life we follow through his journals, we learn about his thoughts and life. You soon meet Mrs Gregorius, a young beautiful woman who is married to a pastor, significant older than her. She goes to doktor Glas about her troubles of carrying out her wifely duties in the bedroom, she is inlove with another man but trapped in a loveless marriage and is basically forced to be intimate with her husband every night. And finally she can't take it anymore so she asks Doktor Glas for help. He comes up with an excuse for Mrs Gregorious to say to her husband that makes it impossible for them to be intimate, but even so the Reverends needs and lust is higher than the doktors orders and again the woman is faced with her fears. Doktor Glas then faces the question; is it right to kill a person to save another?<br /><br />A beautifully written book that really stays with you. I really enjoyed it and it is wonderful to get to read a Swedish classic in its original language (when the most books I read are in English even though I'm Swedish)<br /><br />A very interested subject and a book everyone should read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17617073320929258283" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_66239222" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/66239222" />
    <a title="Anders" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1380499-anders"><img alt="Anders" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1222014470p2/1380499.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/66239222?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anders" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anders" href="/user/show/1380499-anders">Anders</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer66239222" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5123125294568326317">You should, if you are able to of course,read this in Swedish, as the choice of tone is demonstrated and enhanced through the usage of quirky Swedish language from that time,(1905). Beyond a case of obsessive behaviour (as someone posted on here), it's a tale of protest. Protesting authority and an individual representative's abuse of power, manipulation, and control. The outlet for this doctor is to use his version of the same. <br/>A sobering read.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jWqUWi0Y7KcSRB49a423Fqp6fjVHBoqEopkaKP+WjbISNVnV3c8jMsrMhMSHuDC/Ztg31XDKunU/a3FHfX5ZcA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7QI/+sRIFhrnH9tAU87YmqrQv6E3MBfGKnl0d3olGZpyXfJ1NJ/Zjz+XQbm/+18zZnL2QQD8Jze3ix8Y+M3NWA==')})
  }

His consistently faithful depiction of these humbl<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText3593408659631367446\" style=\"display:none\">Considered one of Sweden\'s greatest 20th-century writers, Vilhelm Moberg created Karl Oskar and Kristina Nilsson to portray the joys and tragedies of daily life for early Swedish pioneers in America. His consistently faithful depiction of these humble people\'s lives is a major strength of the Emigrant Novels.Moberg\'s extensive research in the papers of Swedish emigrants in archival collections, including the Minnesota Historical Society, enabled him to incorporate many details of pioneer life. First published between 1949 and 1959 in Swedish, these four books were considered a single work by Moberg, who intended that they be read as documentary novels. These editions contain introductions written by Roger McKnight, Gustavus Adolphus College, and restore Moberg\'s bibliography not included in earlier English editions.Book 1 introduces Karl Oskar and Kristina Nilsson, their three young children, and eleven others who make up a resolute party of Swedes fleeing the poverty, religious persecution, and social oppression of Sm�land in 1850.&quot;It\'s       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/302660.Hjalmar_S_derberg">About Hjalmar Söderberg</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/302660.Hjalmar_S_derberg"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1357615753p3/302660.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/302660.Hjalmar_S_derberg">Hjalmar Söderberg
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
148
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2091862740920038428">Hjalmar Emil Fredrik Söderberg was a Swedish novelist, playwright, poet and journalist. His works often deal with melancholy and lovelorn characters, and offer a rich portrayal of contemporary Stockholm through the eyes of the flaneur. Söderberg is greatly appreciated in his native country, and is sometimes considered to be the equal of August Strindberg, Sweden's national author.</span>

</div>
</div>

<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>

This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
